  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b072df02-39b2-4b1d-8573-5a260f1b6729'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13551121104129974688">Will Scarlet is good at two things: stealing from the rich and keeping secrets - skills that are in high demand in Robin Hood's band of thieves, who protect the people of Nottingham from the evil sheriff. Scarlet's biggest secret of all is one only Robin and his men know...that <i>she</i> is posing as a thief; that the slip of a boy who is fast with sharp knives is really a girl.</span>
  <span id="freeText13551121104129974688" style="display:none">Will Scarlet is good at two things: stealing from the rich and keeping secrets - skills that are in high demand in Robin Hood's band of thieves, who protect the people of Nottingham from the evil sheriff. Scarlet's biggest secret of all is one only Robin and his men know...that <i>she</i> is posing as a thief; that the slip of a boy who is fast with sharp knives is really a girl.<p>The terrible events in her past that led Scarlet to hide her real identity are in danger of being exposed when the thief taker Lord Gisbourne arrives in town to rid Nottingham of the Hood and his men once and for all. As Gisbourne closes in and puts innocent lives at risk, Scarlet must decide how much the people of Nottingham mean to her, especially John Little, a flirtatious fellow outlaw, and Robin, whose quick smiles have the rare power to unsettle her. There is real honor among these thieves and so much more - making this a fight worth dying for.</p></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer857096966" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer217311363634689816"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392618334ra/8584856.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This is an alternate retelling of Robin Hood, where Will Scarlet is a hemorrhoidal pain in the ass who talks like a <i>Monty Python and the Holy Grail</i> cast reject that gets involved in a horrifyingly painful love triangle WITH ROBIN HOOD AND LITTLE JOHN</b>.<br/><br/>There are two facts about Will Scarlet that you should know before starting this book.<br/><br/>1. Will Scarlet is actually a "she," a girl disguised as a boy<br/><br/>2. The "Scarlet" in her name refers to the fact that SHE CAN'T STOP FUCKING BLUSHING*<br/><br/>*That's actually</span>
  <span id="freeText217311363634689816" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392618334ra/8584856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This is an alternate retelling of Robin Hood, where Will Scarlet is a hemorrhoidal pain in the ass who talks like a <i>Monty Python and the Holy Grail</i> cast reject that gets involved in a horrifyingly painful love triangle WITH ROBIN HOOD AND LITTLE JOHN</b>.<br><br>There are two facts about Will Scarlet that you should know before starting this book.<br><br>1. Will Scarlet is actually a "she," a girl disguised as a boy<br><br>2. The "Scarlet" in her name refers to the fact that SHE CAN'T STOP FUCKING BLUSHING*<br><br>*That's actually something I made up, but I wasn't exaggerrating when I say that she blushes like fucking crazy.<br><br><u>Will <b>Blushes</b> Scarlet</u>: OH MY GOD JUST STAAAAHP ALREADY. I wanted to love Scarlet, I really do. A kick-ass heroine who disguises herself as a boy in order to steal from the rich and give to the poor?! FUCK YEAH, give me more of that shit.<br><br>No.<br><br>I admit, <b>there is a fair bit of kick-assery in there, but it feels completely unrealistic becaues Will Scarlet can't decide who or what the fuck she is</b>.<br><br>Is she a kick-ass fighting tomboy?! Or is she a girl whose heart goes aflutter whenever she gets near Robin Hood? So many time in this book, <b>her heart flushes, her heartbeat go pitter-patter, her belly gets butterflies.<br><br>My stomach's content just turned over.</b><br><br>Let's see, <b>blushing...how many instances are there</b>? "I felt heat on my face and hated that the sun would show me blushing," "It were dark, so they couldn’t prove I were blushing," "I blushed," "[I was] cold again but for my cheeks, which were blushing hard," "I were blushing hot," "I felt my cheeks blush," "I blushed hot," "I shake him off, blushing," "I blushed a little," "it sent my cheeks blushing," "I blushed a bit."<br><br>Ok, we've gotten the blushing over with. Now onto the <b>flushing</b>! "I pulled my head away, flushed and not sure what to do, or say, or think," "my cheeks flush," "my cheeks flushed dark," "I flushed," "my cheeks went hot," "blood filled up my cheeks."<br><br>Oh, but the stomach-churning flutterings don't stop there, no! Let's see what other sort of over-extravagant emotion our dauntless fighting girl has in store for us!<br><br><b>"The air whooshed from my chest</b>," "the breath whooshed out of me," "my belly twisted," "my belly flipped over," "my heart started to flutter-beat in my chest," "I got that funny, twisted feeling," "my heart lurched," "my heart dropped out from my chest," "my knees had gone fair wobbling," "my stomach pushed into my pipes."<br><br>Spare me. <b>This book tries to sell me the fact that Scarlet is a fierce warrior; it didn't convince me in the least.</b> Scarlet is ruled by her feelings, she lets her heart win over her head, she gets nervous, she feels tremors, she acts like a silly little girl who was forced into being a warrior instead of a warrior born, instead of one who has chosen her fate.<br><br><u>Scarlet's Personality</u>: Incongruous.<br><br><i>In-con-gru-ous</i>: /adjective/ not in harmony or keeping with the surroundings or other aspects of something.<br><br>That is the single word that can be used to describe Scarlet's personality. She is not a good character. She is an annoying character. She acts like a petulant child instead of a rational, cool-headed warrior. She snaps at people at the very tinest, dumbest provocation.<blockquote>
  <i>“Bugger off,” I snapped.</i>
</blockquote>Scarlet loses her temper extremely fast. She makes some really dumb decisions at times...like rushing off to attack people in broad fucking daylight. There is a way to be subtle, Robin Hood's Merry Men have to stick around awhile in order to accomplish their good deeds, and <b>Scarlet does things with the subtlety of a pink and purple polka-dotted elephant dancing on a unicycle</b>.<br><br><u>Her Speech</u>: I absolutely HATED her first-person narrative. I mentioned that she talks like a Monty Python reject, and she does. It is annoying, it distracts from the already terribly boring narrative, and it makes no fucking sense when you take into consideration who she actually is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maid Marian, a noblewoman <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Her dialogue is pretentious, it is heavy dotted with grammatical inconsistencies, which doesn't feel authentic at all, because in one instance, she talks like a street urchin complete with "ain'ts" and "weren'ts." Her fucking "weren't." "I weren't," "he weren't." Fuck you. <b>It doesn't make any fucking sense because she speaks in horribly accented speech like an uneducated wench...</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Just because you kissed me don’t mean I’m your girl none,” I told him.</i>
</blockquote>Even her very thoughts are sprinkled with terrible grammar, only to have her turn out to be who she is...<b>Scarlet's character completely reeks of artifice.</b><br><br>It seems like Scarlet is the only one who speaks like that in the entire book. The other characters are seemingly no better off than she is, they're a bunch of ragtag men, after all, but their speech is all perfectly normal, without any pretensions to be anything lower or more crass. <b>The inconsistency of Scarlet's dialogue and thoughts in contrast to the other "normal guys" only serves to make her more of an utterly unconvincing character</b>.<br><br><u>Her Fighting Skills</u>: HOW THE FUCK DID SHE GET THEM?! We see her fight. A lot. She kicks ass. She dresses as a boy, she dresses down some boys. There's no disputing that the girl can fight. BUT HOW?! Once her history is mentioned, it makes even less sense. How does such a girl become such a fierce fighter, in such a short time? It makes no fucking sense, and I don't buy it. I respect that she is a good fighter, but you have to convince me that she is one, I don't want a character to magically become an awesome fighter just because. Give me a fucking reason. Show me her training. Tell me <b>WHY</b> I should respect her and how Scarlet became who she is today. This book brings me in cold as to her history, and it continues to leave me in the dark.<br><br><u>The Setting</u>: This book does a fucking terrible job of giving us a setting. <b>It truly is one of the worst excuses for a historical book I have ever read</b>. WHAT SETTING? We're in the past, but rather than an actual time period, this book has the feel of anything from...say, Crusade-era to, I don't know....mid-19th century England.<br><br><b>I could only tell it was England due to the fact that "London" was mentioned. This is one of those times when I longed for purple prose and long descriptions, because there were none in this book.</b><br><br>This book was all action and more action and not much more than that. There is no clear descriptions of anything. No descriptions about the dress. Few descriptions about the people. I couldn't even begin to tell you what the fuck Robin and John looked like. There was no sense of time other than the brief mention of "Oh, I went to the Crusades blah blah years ago." Ok, we're in the time of the Crusades. IS THAT ALL? GIVE ME SOME MORE DETAILS, FOR FUCK'S SAKES. Christ on a cracker.<br><br>Let me give you a description. The Templar flag is that of a red cross on a white background. Do you like that? That's more description than most anything you get from this fucking book. It could have taken place in 19th century backwoods of England, for all that matters. <b>There is no sense of time, no sense of place, no atmosphere whatsoever to this book.</b><br><br>One other thing that bothered me about this book: Robin, the Earl, is referred to as "your grace," because of his status as the Earl. Correct me if I'm wrong, but "your grace" is an honorary address for a duke, right?<br><br><u>The Love Triangle</u>: FUCK THAT SHIT. Robin Hood would fucking NEVER. WHY?! I mean, really, WHY?!<br><br>There should be no fucking time for romance when the Sheriff is corrupt, and threatening to string up your entire town for not paying the taxes.<blockquote>
  <i>Did he think I were John’s bit of fun for the day? My belly twisted and I didn’t like the feeling.<br>And he weren’t Rob. But then, maybe that weren’t such an awful thing. Rob’s sort I could never deserve.</i>
</blockquote>There should be no fucking time for romance when the Thief Hunter is burning up your hideout and threatening to decapitate the people in your town for hiding your identity.<blockquote>
  <i>His eyes looked into mine in a way that made my breath suck out of my pipes. “You’re every kind of surprise, you know that?”</i>
</blockquote>There should be no fucking time for romance when there is a traitor in town who is threatening to destroy all you hold dear.<blockquote>
  <i>He looked at me, his eyes running over my face. He came closer, and I were against the wall, so my heart started to flutter-beat in my chest. I didn’t much like feeling trapped. He palmed my hat, pushing it back.<br>“What are you doing?” I asked, pulling away.<br>“I need to see your eyes when I ask you this.”<br>“Ask what?”<br>“Are you in love with Rob, Scar?”</i>
</blockquote>There's no fucking time for romance when you are on the run, hiding from a man who's out for your blood.<blockquote>
  <i>His lips pressed against mine, strong like the rest of him and a little wet, pushing my lips into a fair good kiss. He caught me up ’bout the waist and kissed me deeper. I shut my eyes, and Rob’s face popped into my head.</i>
</blockquote>Most of all, THERE SHOULD BE NO FUCKING TIME FOR A LOVE TRIANGLE WHEN YOU ARE SUPPOSED TO FUCKING TRUST AND BEFRIEND ONE ANOTHER. ROBIN HOOD'S MERRY MEN DO NOT FIGHT AMONG ONE ANOTHER FOR A GIRL'S FUCKING EVER-CHANGING HEART.<blockquote>
  <i>“About John,” he said at long last.<br>I blinked.<br>“I don’t want to know how you two are fooling about, but if it interferes with the band I’ll kick you out myself.”</i>
</blockquote>This was just a terrible book. There is too much action without much else. There is no subtlety to the plot. Characters are thrown about as if they were nothing, characters were introduced haphazardly, as needed. This was just a very poorly thought out book.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="217311363634689816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_289445466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289445466" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2649065-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561941236p2/2649065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289445466?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/2649065-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Foxes</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=bland-romance">bland-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=ehhhhh">ehhhhh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=didn-t-make-sense">didn-t-make-sense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=gorgeous-cover">gorgeous-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2649065-claire?shelf=had-potential">had-potential</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289445466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8453732007715953285">I don't know about anyone else but when I think of Robin Hood I think of this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435903235ra/15386799.gif' width='400' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Wait, I'm the only one who pictured him like that? Huh. Blame my childhood.<br/>Anyway, when I first started reading this book I admittedly imagined Robin Hood as being pretty hot. Like a total fox. (GET IT?!) <br/>Granted, the Robin Hood in this story was not the main character. Rather, the main character was a young woman who everyone knew as Scarlet. Her identity is mysterious and only a few people know that she's secretly a </span>
  <span id="freeText8453732007715953285" style="display:none">I don't know about anyone else but when I think of Robin Hood I think of this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435903235ra/15386799.gif" width="400" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Wait, I'm the only one who pictured him like that? Huh. Blame my childhood.<br>Anyway, when I first started reading this book I admittedly imagined Robin Hood as being pretty hot. Like a total fox. (GET IT?!) <br>Granted, the Robin Hood in this story was not the main character. Rather, the main character was a young woman who everyone knew as Scarlet. Her identity is mysterious and only a few people know that she's secretly a girl. She's tough, smart, brave, and completely capable of taking care of herself. She's a hardcore, kick-butt girl living in the Middle Ages. Or at least that's how I think the author wanted her to come off as. In reality she's kind of a whiny jerk to everyone. When people try to be genuinely nice to her she's completely rude and pushes them away. I couldn't stand her character. She was ill-mannered and unappreciative. I guess she was supposed to seem really independent but instead she just seemed stuck up and full of it. Maybe she wasn't as bad as I'm making her out to be, but there were plenty of times where I actually wanted to go into the book and strangle her. <br>I also got really annoyed at the way Scarlet talked. She didn't use proper grammar at all, despite the rest of the Merry Men have perfect grammar. And that would have bothered me except <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she's actually Maid Marian <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It's eventually revealed that she grew up as a privileged lady. So why is her grammar terrible?! You would think her grammar would be loads better than everyone else's, as she lived in an upper class society. But noooooo. Maybe I shouldn't be fussing over that little detail this much but it seriously got on my nerves since she had been raised with nobles. <br>Scarlet was also too selfless. She kept trying to sacrifice herself to save others. Which hey, heroes are good! But it was too the point where she just seemed like an idiot. Like her sacrifices were suicidal and it was like she was trying too hard to play the martyr. She had no common sense. Like she refused to eat because there were people in the town starving. Okay, because you can totally help them when your dying of hunger. That makes about as much sense as, well - <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435903472ra/15386835.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>You know what else I hated about this book? <b>The Dreaded Love Triangle.</b> It was completely and utterly unnecessary. It was the thing that bothered me the most in this entire book. So in the love triangle, we've got Scarlet, Little John, and Robin Hood. Robin Hood clearly has feelings for Scarlet but she's in denial. Little John suddenly decides he's attracted to her and she starts responding to him, despite the fact that he admits that he's not serious about it. Robin meanwhile turns all jealous but rather then admitting to Scarlet that it's because he's in love with her, he gives her the cold shoulder and threatens to kick her out of the group. Real smart, fox-boy. <br>She swears that she has no interest in Little John. So why do you keep cuddling and kissing him, Scarlet? Huh? She keeps leading on Little John and Robin Hood and then acts shocked when they get mad at her. At this point, I was getting more than a little peeved a at Scarlet.. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435903016ra/15386784.gif" width="500" height="289" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Also, I don't know why she was even conflicting about all this! If she claimed that she had no interest in Little John, then why did she keep showing him affection? Not to mention that he's a total jerk to everyone. Robin Hood was at least a gentlemen at the beginning (before he turned all angsty). Little John is just mean. What I want to wonder if why the author chose Little John to be apart of the love triangle. Maybe it's just me, but when I picture Little John I think of this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435902883ra/15386776.gif" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Because dancing bears are the definition of sexy </i><br>Plus we all knew she was going to end up with Robin. Little John was just an unnecessary distraction. It was really predictable. The Little John subplot was a ruse! This is what I was about ready to do to that 'love triangle': <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435904277ra/15386929.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yep.<br>Okay, so I suppose I should go into what I liked about the book. Because, contrary to my previous rambling, I didn't hate the book. It was more of a 2.5 rating but technically it got three stars. The plot was well-paced and fairly exciting. It wasn't slow or tedious. The writing style flowed enough that I was able to read it easily so kudos to that. And the entire cast of characters weren't all that bad. They weren't perfect but I occasionally felt compassion for them. <br>There's one other thing about this book that I feel like I should mention. <br>Guy of Gisbourne. <br>Yeah, yeah, I know I was supposed to hate him. He was supposed to be a cruel, evil, horrible being that murdered innocent beings. Is it so bad that I wanted him to turn from the dark ways because he was actually in love with Scarlet? I'm a total sucker for bad-guys-who-fall-for-good-girls. Especially when it causes them to question their moral beliefs. I actually loved the part where Scarlet calls him a monster and he yells that she made him a monster, and that he's been desperately searching for her for many years. I honestly wanted them to fall in love, after he changed his psycho murderer ways of course. Don't judge me! I watched BBC's Robin Hood series. When I pictured Guy of Gisbourne I imagined this:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435904008ra/15386875.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Mmmm, Richard Armitage...</i><br>Apparently I'm insane because that never went down. Guy vanishes once Scarlet and the Merry Men defeat him and all is well. The climax was a bit confusing to me. One moment she's marrying Guy and the next she's running all over the place and being a ninja. At times I wasn't really sure what the blazes was going on. Oh well. In the end, Guy just runs off and the Merry Men have won. Huzzah! And then Scarlet and Robin Hood finally wind up together and it ends a little something like this: <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435903344ra/15386813.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Well, more or less. They didn't really get married. And they may or may not have been foxes.</i><br> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8453732007715953285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2063322895?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>,

<div id="review_262295729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262295729" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262295729?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=historical-fictions">historical-fictions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=arc-e-galley">arc-e-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262295729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15533568257839569606"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet' title='Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a> is wrenching and moving story of love and friendship, bravery and loyalty, a retelling of the legend of Robin Hood, only the voice of narration was Scarlet. Yes Will Scarlet, the most skilled knife- handling young fellow of Robin, in the traditional tales, famous for his hot temper. But he’s not actually what we think he is. He’s no lad; he’s a lass; a girl hiding her true identity in men’s cloth.<br/> <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367421i/719948._SX540_.png' width='500' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Being a part of the merry men, Scarlet was always successful to hide the truth from rest of</span>
  <span id="freeText15533568257839569606" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet" title="Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> is wrenching and moving story of love and friendship, bravery and loyalty, a retelling of the legend of Robin Hood, only the voice of narration was Scarlet. Yes Will Scarlet, the most skilled knife- handling young fellow of Robin, in the traditional tales, famous for his hot temper. But he’s not actually what we think he is. He’s no lad; he’s a lass; a girl hiding her true identity in men’s cloth.<br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380367421i/719948._SX540_.png" width="500" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Being a part of the merry men, Scarlet was always successful to hide the truth from rest of the Nottingham; of course her companions knew about her. Now the evil thief taker Sir Guy of Gisbourne is terrorizing the Village with violence and fury; determine to catch Robin. But Scarlet knew what he is actually after. It’s her and Guy will not stop until he possessed her and crushed her to the dust. Her secrets threatened to disentangle; painful memories of past are about to unravel that can change everything in present.<br><br><b>Scarlet Fever</b><br><br>Disguised as a boy, <b>Scarlet</b> is secretive, impulsive, strong and mysterious, no less in any quality than an actual lad. She’s one of the bravest and toughest female protagonists I have ever came across, no wonder why Robin called her a worrier woman. Scarlet was Invulnerable to fear or intimidation. She faced and withstands Gisbourne with courage. She helped the people of Nottingham the best she could, she fought for justice alongside Robin, John and Much. She may have a tough exterior, but her interior was made with delicate glass just like an eighteen years old girl, which shattered with each piercing word came from Robin and melted in warm embrace of the same person. As a reader, above all as a girl I was empathetic to her pain and adopted them as mine. Sometime it was really hard for me to hold back my tears. Her feeling and affection was strong for Rob, but the ultimate sacrifice she made to save the person she loved was praise worthy. <br>I know the readers have already begun to guess about Scar, but if you think I’m going tell you her true identity, sorry to say I will not spoil this enchanting historical story. <br><br><b>The Walking Ghost</b><br><br><i>
  <b>“You changed everything. Everything. That day in the market in London, you don’t know what my life was like before that, when I came home and found everything just gone. I had nothing. I hadn’t a soul. And then you appeared with your magic eyes, and you just changed everything.”</b>
</i><br><br><b>Robin Hood</b>, the legendary character, angel to poor, one of the most famous archers in history was just Rob for Scarlet, and I fall in love with him too. A retired heart from Cursed devoted his youth in novel cause to serve people, to save them from being tortured by sheriff, In the process accompanied by a girl with eyes color of moonstone, Rob found himself caring for that brave and rude girl. <br>Hurting Scar was the best way to punish himself, and of course Rob was not very proud of that. In spite of every effort he made to deny his own feelings for Scar, I could see the warm compassionate feelings in his stormy eyes. Out of all the things he had done, he loved her more, protected Scar with all his life and knocked down every danger intend to hurt her.<br><br><b>The Merry Men</b><br><br>Right hand of Robin and an excellent swordsman <b>Little John</b> had always been a charmer and he charmed me as well. I liked how the author painted his character with colors of fun and sincerity in equal measure. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet" title="Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> is definitely not a love triangle but John’s growing fondness and likeness for her spiced up the story a little bit. He’s appearance throughout the whole story was remarkable. When it came to loyalty and devotion to Robin and his band, no one was fierce as him. <br><b>Much</b> was always like a brother to Scarlet, the only person Scarlet was most comfortable with. Sometime I felt sympathy for him, but he proved he doesn’t need anyone’s sympathy. In spite of having one good arm, Much has a quality of spirit and will power that enabled him to fight. <br><br>As a debut author A.C. Gaughen brought us that secrets and hidden fact behind one of the most famous legend of history. Sometime untold truth buried beneath the history, we just need to dig that deep. The writing was very touching and mesmerizing that I applaud her efforts. The ending was completely unexpected and my heart skipped a bit. Series of turns and twists, secrets and actions, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet" title="Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> will leave you speechless. This book is Capable of arousing and holding the attention. <br><br>I have been searching around trying to figure out if this was a stand alone or a series? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet" title="Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a> left lots of question running in my mind. I am hoping that this will be a series because I would love to read more about the romance and where it turns from here. <b>But right now I’m down with Scarlet fever. Are you?</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15533568257839569606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_278891405" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278891405" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278891405?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=steampunk-historical">steampunk-historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=whiny-annoying-blah-heroine">whiny-annoying-blah-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278891405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9629668155395286503"><b>1.5 stars</b><br/><br/>A retelling of Robin Hood where Will Scarlet, a member of Robin's band is a actually girl in disguise.<br/>-The storyline didn't really entertain me, it was boring and the real action only really kicked in towards the end.<br/>-The narrative was strange, it was part present tense and part past tense, I couldn't get my head around it.<br/>-The British-isms and British slang didn't read right AT ALL, it felt forced and it made me cringe at how hard it tried to sound authentically British.<br/>-The love trian</span>
  <span id="freeText9629668155395286503" style="display:none"><b>1.5 stars</b><br /><br />A retelling of Robin Hood where Will Scarlet, a member of Robin's band is a actually girl in disguise.<br />-The storyline didn't really entertain me, it was boring and the real action only really kicked in towards the end.<br />-The narrative was strange, it was part present tense and part past tense, I couldn't get my head around it.<br />-The British-isms and British slang didn't read right AT ALL, it felt forced and it made me cringe at how hard it tried to sound authentically British.<br />-The love triangle was annoying and not needed.<br />-Worst of all, the three main characters were awful:<br /><b>Scarlet</b><br />Good god I hated this heroine. She was meant to be brave, strong and compassionate..and truthfully she was but it was hard to appreciate any of the good in her when it was overshadowed by all the bad. Scarlet was annoying, self pitying and whiny. She starved herself because she felt guilty that others were going hungry, even though she stole everyday so she could help feed the poorer families. Why she thought going hungry would help anyone..the poorer families relied on her, Robin and co to provide for them, so I don't know why she thought her dying of starvation would help anyone. <br />Scarlet was too much of a martyr, she was too self-sacrificing, she felt responsible for everyone, she felt guilty about things she had no control over..OMG I felt like throttling her. When she rescues someone from prison, she lets the guy beat her black and blue because she didn't save said guy's sister sooner. It wasn't her fault they were in prison in the first place or that she wasn't able to save the sister sooner but on no Scarlet blames herself, feels guilty and is happy to get beaten up because she thinks she deserves it. I got tried of how Scarlet felt like she was personally responsible for everyone and their mother.<br />I despised when Scarlet said she hated being a woman. I like my heroines to be proud to be a woman.<br />Scarlet had hardly any self worth and she punished herself about everything..how was I meant to like/love a character when the character didn't even like themselves, not even a little bit.<br /><b>Robin</b><br />He was quiet a good love interest initally - dark, brooding and noble but his attitude towards Scarlet and John pissed me off. Robin blames Scarlet for leading John on and teasing him, when it was John doing all the chasing but oh no he doesn't have a go at John..because it's all Scarlet's fault that John has a hard on for her..it has nothing to do with the fact that Johns a disgusting, dirty pervert who likes to perv. He also calls Scarlet a whore!! Why because John kissed her and because her father forced her to be engaged to another man when she was 13/14 years old..WTF?! I find it really interesting that in a lot of books that I've read over the last couple of years, the heroine is called a whore/slut/skank by the hero (who by the way has slept with loads of girls) when she's actually a virgin and has very little experience in general with men!!<br /><b>John</b><br />John was a typical playboy, he openly slept with many <i>wenches</i> and flirted with anyone with a pulse..John suddenly decided he wanted Scarlet and for some unfathomable reason thought he had some sort of claim on her. He kissedScarlet when it's clear she wasn't interested in him and he kept coming onto her when she was vulnerable. He also got angry when he thought Scarlet was with someone else even though it was ok for him to sleep around..he also conveniantly forgot Scarlet was free to be with whoever she wanted. I'm sick of the playboy love interests..I don't find them attractive in the least.<br />I did like Much, he was a great little character.<br />Overall it just wasn't my cup of tea..if you like Robin Hood, faux Britishness, annoying heroines, judgemental heroes, a playboy third wheel and a weak love triangle then you might just enjoy this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9629668155395286503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2484134587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484134587" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484134587?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=robin-hood">robin-hood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484134587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16263862674208293933"><b>"Make no mistake," he told me. I looked up. "We do what we do-" He halted, then stepped one foot closer. "I do what I do because I will always believe that no matter how awful life gets for however many of these people, there is something I can do about it. There is something I will do about it."<br/> I nodded. "That's why you're the hero, Rob, and I'm a thief."</b><br/><br/>Robin Hood <b>stole my heart</b> at a really young age. As a matter of fact, <i>this hunk</i> was my <b>first ever crush</b>…<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553895201ra/27287376.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Isn’t he just divine??? <i>Sigh…</i> Too bad</span>
  <span id="freeText16263862674208293933" style="display:none"><b>"Make no mistake," he told me. I looked up. "We do what we do-" He halted, then stepped one foot closer. "I do what I do because I will always believe that no matter how awful life gets for however many of these people, there is something I can do about it. There is something I will do about it."<br> I nodded. "That's why you're the hero, Rob, and I'm a thief."</b><br><br>Robin Hood <b>stole my heart</b> at a really young age. As a matter of fact, <i>this hunk</i> was my <b>first ever crush</b>…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553895201ra/27287376.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isn’t he just divine??? <i>Sigh…</i> Too bad it was 1938 when this was filmed. <i>NO FAIR</i>. He should’ve <b>waited for me</b> to be born! Pfft. :P<br><br>Anyway, in this interpretation of Robin Hood, we see <b>Earl Robin of Locksley</b> (obviously), <b>“Will” Scarlet</b> (who is – in fact – a girl disguised as a boy), <b>John Little</b>, and <b>Much</b>. Why do we never see the other Merry Men in retellings?! Hopefully, we’ll see them the future instalments.<br><br><i>"You lied to me tonight," John said. <br>I shrugged. "I lie to you a lot. Reckon you might want to be more specific." <br>"You said you'd wait at the top. You said we'd go together." <br>"Well, yes, that was a lie."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553895201ra/27287377.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Either way, <b>Scar</b>’s incessant blushing at the most inappropriate of times was irritating after a while, but it didn’t really affect my <b>enjoyment of her character</b>. She has a <i>secret past</i>, an affinity for daggers and is <b>the most capable thief</b> of the Merry Men. She has a hardened personality and acts like “one of the boys.” As “Will” Scarlet, many think her <i>merely a boy</i>, and she uses that assumption to her advantage. But despite her <b>sassy</b> and hardened exterior, she’s also very <i>caring and generous</i>. In true Robin Hood fashion, she helps those around her who cannot help themselves in the village of Nottingham and Sherwood Forest. I found her to be an <b>admirable protagonist</b>. Scar is also hiding from those in her past, who seek to do her harm. I also predicted her past from a mile away, but I enjoyed the reveal at the end, nonetheless!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1553895201ra/27287378.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Rob</b>, more commonly referred to as “The Hood”, was naturally my favourite character. I don’t know what it is that I find <b>so attractive</b> about him, but whether he be in a book or on a screen, I’m guaranteed to <b>fall in love</b> with him, haha. Rob is the leader of the Merry Men, stealing from the rich, giving to the poor, and freeing the innocent from imprisonment. He is <i>kind and giving</i>, and at times, a <b>jealous arsehole</b> because he simply won’t admit how he feels to Scar. <i>UGH!</i> <b>Communication, people!</b> And I’m sorry, <b>John Little</b>, you’re nice and all, but stop getting in the way of my ship! <i>B A C K!!! O F F!!!</i><br><br><i>She shook her head. "They would have pinched you too, and then where would Robin be?" <br>"He'd be right as rain, I think." <br>She chuckled. "You don't see how much he cares about you, but he does. Ran into that fire last night like a fair angel, he did."<br> "He'd do the same for one of his men, or any of his people. Don't make me special in his eyes." It were shameful, but there were a fair amount of bitter in my voice. <br>She leaned her head close to mine so the others wouldn't overhear her. "Ah, he has many men, but he only has one woman."</i><br><br> I can’t believe I’m saying this, but I did genuinely enjoy the <b>angst and jealousy</b> in this book. Usually, these tropes get on my nerves, but I was all here for it!!! Gimme some more!!! Scar and Rob made me nearly <b>scream and cry</b>, but I enjoyed <i>every moment</i> of it!!! They kept me glued to the novel because I was <i>SO INVESTED</i> in them, their relationship, and the everything going up in flames around them. Seriously, things kept going from <b>bad to worse</b> and I was an <b>emotional mess</b> by the time I reached the end of the novel. What a compelling read! <br><br>I’d also like to note that the <b>writing style</b> was a tad difficult to get into, at first. It was written in – I don’t know…<b>peasant English</b>? Instead of “<i>isn’t</i>”, “<i>ain’t</i>” is used. Rather than “<i>he is</i>”, “<i>he were</i>” is written. This made me a bit iffy when I began the novel, as I prefer proper English, but as I read more and more, I <b>stopped noticing it</b>, so it wasn’t as big as an issue for me as I thought it would be.   <br><br>Needless to say, <i>I LOVED THIS!!!</i> This trilogy should get <b>more hype</b>, in my opinion. I didn’t even mind <b>Sir Guy of Gisbourne</b> and the <b>Sheriff of Nottingham</b>, despite my hatred of them, haha. Where was <b>Prince John</b> though? I heard mentions of him, but didn’t see him at all in the book! I hope that we’ll see him and <b>King Richard the Lionheart</b> soon! :) <br><br><i>THIS</i> is what I wanted from a <b>Robin Hood retelling</b>!!! I can’t wait to binge the rest of the trilogy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16263862674208293933" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_381928525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381928525" />
    <a title="Duckie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3583211-duckie"><img alt="Duckie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354537526p2/3583211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381928525?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duckie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duckie" href="/user/show/3583211-duckie">Duckie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13482635-scarlet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3583211-duckie?shelf=hoodwinkers">hoodwinkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3583211-duckie?shelf=biblio-bile">biblio-bile</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381928525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3437450689216237023">This is the first time I've read a version of the Robin Hood story where I wanted the sheriff to win. Flimsy characters, clunky writing and gaping plot holes mangle what otherwise might have been a decent YA novel.<br/><br/>The narrative is in Scarlet's voice but it's pretty hard to tell what that is, exactly. It's vaguely British and vaguely working-class but is rooted in neither Yorkshire nor London, where she claims to be from at different points in the novel. Like the plot, it also shows up when it fe</span>
  <span id="freeText3437450689216237023" style="display:none">This is the first time I've read a version of the Robin Hood story where I wanted the sheriff to win. Flimsy characters, clunky writing and gaping plot holes mangle what otherwise might have been a decent YA novel.<br><br>The narrative is in Scarlet's voice but it's pretty hard to tell what that is, exactly. It's vaguely British and vaguely working-class but is rooted in neither Yorkshire nor London, where she claims to be from at different points in the novel. Like the plot, it also shows up when it feels like it and then fades away when it thinks no one is looking. Scarlet's voice is distinct from the other characters only because they all speak like Americans, which is another problem altogether. I don't have a problem with first-person narratives that use bad English, if it's in character, but it doesn't work if the grammar is sometimes bad and sometimes perfect, or if none of the other characters are speaking in dialect.<br><br>Also, Scarlet showers her narrative with tense changes like Robin Hood scattering gold to the villagers. She jumps from past tense, to past perfect, to present tense and back again; there's so much jumping around in time, I expected to see a TARDIS pop out of Sherwood.<br><br>Scarlet is whiny, annoying and a consummate Mary Sue. She prattles on about how she's great at stealing and the only proper thief of the bunch, but her thieving skills are on par with an unattended toddler in a toy store. She sees something she wants, waits until the owner is looking the other direction, and grabs it. Wow, mad skillz yo.<br><br>Scarlet also boasts that she's needed because only she can pick out the good marks. Like she can spot nobles traveling in disguise because they're riding destriers instead of farm horses. Here's a test. This is a destrier:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386104i/745347.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is a farm horse:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386104i/745348.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>Can you see the difference? Good, because apparently a bunch of dudes born and raised in a farming community can't. Presumably Scarlet then went on to remind them how to breathe.<br><br>Scarlet also has ninja skills. This is never explained. WTF.<br><br>The writing careens between being too vague and channeling Captain Obvious. Take this quote for example:<br><br>"The man pulled out the knife as his counterpart unsheathed his big sword. Swords are terrible. They are naught but big, heavy knives that most don't know how to use right."<br><br>I read that twice thinking "Well yeah, swords are terrible, that's why you try to avoid the pointy end" before realizing she meant "swords are <i>terrible weapons for other people to use.</i>" I'm not even going to discuss the fact that this guard pulled out a sword (short-range weapon) while she was throwing knives (mid-range weapon). That's like being charged by someone with a pistol and hoping they get close enough for you to use your bowstave.<br><br>And then there's this:<br><br>"I walked down slow, seeing the rough, carved-out wall. It were wet with water."<br><br>Wow, and here I was thinking it was wet with a nice 1196 Bordeaux from the kegger upstairs.<br><br>This was followed later by:<br><br>"John looked to me, and I felt his eyes on me."<br><br>Probably because he was looking at you. Which you just mentioned. Right there. I mean, it's in the same freaking line.<br><br>And then there's Robin Hood's line:<br><br>"I had nothing. I hadn't a soul. And then you appeared with your magic eyes, and you just changed everything."<br><br>OK there's nothing grammatically incorrect with that, but- Magic eyes, people. MAGIC EYES.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386104ra/745349.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The plot moves at a decent pace, but even this puts me in mind of the joke about mail delivery: "If you want to send something, FedEx will get it there by 10AM tomorrow, UPS will get it there, and the Postal Service will get it...somewhere." This novel is the USPS of YA literature. It moves, yes, but it's not sure where it's going, and I'm not even sure I'd like it to arrive there. It honestly surprised me when I read that the author had attended a graduate program in creative writing. I've seen fanfiction written by high schoolers that was better than this.<br><br>Bottom line: If you've seen the 2006-2009 BBC Robin Hood series, you've already seen everything in this story done, and done better. If you haven't seen it, save yourself a few bucks and hours of facepalming and watch that instead.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3437450689216237023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_140831461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140831461" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140831461?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who want to read about Robin Hood finally meeting his match heroine-wise</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=glad-i-gave-it-a-chance">glad-i-gave-it-a-chance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroines-i-love-and-or-admire">heroines-i-love-and-or-admire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this">wish-i-could-write-a-book-like-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=distinctive-voice-narratives">distinctive-voice-narratives</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140831461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13107873793390136522">(<b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5 stars)<br/><br/><i>"We do what we do because there's something we can do about it. Things like 'how long' and 'what if' aren't part of that. It's about the hope, not the horror."</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet' title='Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Scarlet</a>, 2012 debut novel from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4573275.A_C__Gaughen' title='A.C. Gaughen' rel='nofollow noopener'>A.C. Gaughen</a>, takes the legends and characters associated with Robin Hood and spins them all into an engrossing story focusing on a secretive thief who's much more than meets the eye. The people of Nottinghamshire know the thief as Will Scarlet, knife-wielding companion to Robin Hood</span>
  <span id="freeText13107873793390136522" style="display:none">(<b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5 stars)<br /><br /><i>"We do what we do because there's something we can do about it. Things like 'how long' and 'what if' aren't part of that. It's about the hope, not the horror."</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11983940.Scarlet" title="Scarlet by A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">Scarlet</a>, 2012 debut novel from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4573275.A_C__Gaughen" title="A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">A.C. Gaughen</a>, takes the legends and characters associated with Robin Hood and spins them all into an engrossing story focusing on a secretive thief who's much more than meets the eye. The people of Nottinghamshire know the thief as Will Scarlet, knife-wielding companion to Robin Hood, but there's a secret few people realize: <i>he</i> is actually a <i>she</i>. Why does Scarlet insist on dressing like a boy? What is her true identity? And why, after two years working alongside Robin, does she still keep secrets from him and the others in the band of outlaws? When her past begins to stalk her in the form of villainous thief taker Gisbourne, terrorizing the people of Nottinghamshire, her secrets threaten to unravel...and, once they're out in the open, nothing will ever be the same.<br /><br />What immediately struck me when I began <i>Scarlet</i> was the <i>voice</i> of the narration. It felt authentic and true to the era (the time of the Crusades) while also managing to remain consistent throughout the story. I haven't been so impressed with the voice of a novel since reading Moira Young's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9917938.Blood_Red_Road__Dustlands___1_" title="Blood Red Road (Dustlands, #1) by Moira Young" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Red Road</a> earlier this year.<br /><br />What also makes this novel notable is Scarlet, a flawed heroine who can be brash, impulsive, rude, unapologetic, and secretive...yet she feels real and relatable because of her flaws. When she finds herself caught between her admiration for Robin and fellow band member John Little's growing interest in her, Scarlet doesn't know how to react, though she never lets any man's interest define or tether her. She has much more to worry about than love problems, and she acts accordingly, helping the people of Nottinghamshire the best she can even though they don't always react kindly to her help.<br /><br />As for the other characters, I found myself loving some of them (Scarlet, obviously; Much, the one-handed boy who feels useless in Robin's band) and being exasperated with others (Robin, who's often surprisingly self-loathing; John, whose interactions with Scarlet teeter between humorous and off-putting). While I loved Scarlet as a strong heroine, a part of me wished that there had been another lead female character to balance her out and make Robin's band seem less of a "boy's club" to which Scarlet was the only girl brave and "special" enough to take part. Sure, we meet other female characters who are strong in their own rights (Lena, the innkeeper; Ravenna, a girl who wants to save her family from poverty; and a nameless noblewomen who proves helpful to Robin's band's cause), but all of them seem almost foils to show Scarlet as "the woman who's different." (You'll understand what I mean by that if you read the novel.) As trite as my issue sounds, it bothered me and hindered some of my enjoyment of the story.<br /><br />Even so, fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5339.Robin_McKinley" title="Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin McKinley</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8596.Tamora_Pierce" title="Tamora Pierce" rel="nofollow noopener">Tamora Pierce</a> will likely find much to love about <i>Scarlet</i>. It's the kind of novel that would seem right at home wedged alongside <i>The Blue Sword</i> and <i>The Song of the Lioness</i> quartet. Though undoubtedly the novel has its fair share of flaws, most of them are easily overlooked because of the charm and character the story contains.<br /><br />The only other real issue I have with the novel is that, as a standalone, <i>Scarlet</i> is ultimately a bit unsatisfying. Will there be a companion or sequel novel on the horizon? One can only hope because the adventures of the Sherwood band seem far from over (and, by the end, I didn't want them to be over).<br /><br />In the end, I recommend <i>Scarlet</i> to anyone who feels wanting for a novel spotlighting a strong, flawed heroine because, as strange as it seems, such girls are hard to find in recent young adult novels. Scarlet managed to tug at my heartstrings, so I can only hope that she'll do the same for anyone who decides to delve into her tale.<br /><br /><i>Note: I received an advanced copy of this book from the publisher through NetGalley.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13107873793390136522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239113139?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly Sabatini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly Sabatini" href="/user/show/1218946-kimberly-sabatini">Kimberly Sabatini</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1218946-kimberly-sabatini?shelf=mg-ya">mg-ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239113139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7177114106129443356">OMG!!!! I loved this book. I'm going to start this review by announcing something that I NEVER expected to say (John--if you're reading this you should close your eyes and skip ahead) ROBIN HOOD IS MY NEW BOYFRIEND!!!! There, it's out in the open. Phew--I feel better now. I know that once you read this--you're going to want him too--but just remember I said it first and this post is time-stamped. But don't worry, you don't have to be turned away empty handed--Rob's band of Merry Men are pretty d</span>
  <span id="freeText7177114106129443356" style="display:none">OMG!!!! I loved this book. I'm going to start this review by announcing something that I NEVER expected to say (John--if you're reading this you should close your eyes and skip ahead) ROBIN HOOD IS MY NEW BOYFRIEND!!!! There, it's out in the open. Phew--I feel better now. I know that once you read this--you're going to want him too--but just remember I said it first and this post is time-stamped. But don't worry, you don't have to be turned away empty handed--Rob's band of Merry Men are pretty darn lovable too.<br /><br />Then there's Scarlet, who is the only one that I'll let date my new boyfriend--because I like her that much. You are going to adore her journey as you read along. It starts with Scarlet, but you'll find it woven through the whole story-- AC Gaughen is a master of writing perfectly balanced characters. I give her my "Friday Night Lights Award" for making me find something redeemable and maybe even likable in ALMOST everyone. <br /><br />Hang on, there's more to love about this book.<br /><br />Lets take a minute to examine the unique plot twists and the creative take on a story that has been done a million times.There was nothing stale about this tale. THIS IS THE ROBIN HOOD THAT I'VE ALWAYS WANTED! I love when I walk away from a great book knowing that that even though the story is fiction, the characters and their journey have become real. But even though I'm girlie gushing--make no mistakes--I'm picking up my own copy to read to my three boys because they are going to love it!!! There is palm-sweating, boy-loving, action and adventure too. This book is going to capture the attention of a broad audience and deservedly so. <br /><br />So proud to be in the Class of 2k12 with AC Gaughen and SCARLET. &lt;3 What are you waiting for--GO READ SCARLET!!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7177114106129443356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
