<div id="review_853671216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/853671216" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/853671216?book_show_action=true">Feb 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=serious-cliffhanger">serious-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer853671216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8979454052844051965"><b>*Re-read for tomoorrrroowwwww!!*</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>His hands came on either side of my face, holding me up to him. Waves were crashing in his eyes, sure and strong and sweeping. "You are my whole heart, Scarlet. And this is breaking it."</i>
</b><br/><br/>I don't know. I don't know <b>how</b> I came across this or <b>why</b> it spoke to me...but it did. Even today I am still giddy and weightless when I think about this book. How amazing is it when you find something that, while it seems intriguing, doesn't necessarily scream, 'You will love m</span>
  <span id="freeText8979454052844051965" style="display:none"><b>*Re-read for tomoorrrroowwwww!!*</b><br><br><br><b>
  <i>His hands came on either side of my face, holding me up to him. Waves were crashing in his eyes, sure and strong and sweeping. "You are my whole heart, Scarlet. And this is breaking it."</i>
</b><br><br>I don't know. I don't know <b>how</b> I came across this or <b>why</b> it spoke to me...but it did. Even today I am still giddy and weightless when I think about this book. How amazing is it when you find something that, while it seems intriguing, doesn't necessarily scream, 'You will love me' and you kind of put it off for months, years, whatever, but then the minute you pick it up it's like...<b>
  <i>Click.</i>
</b> Click, Robin Hood is fucking sexy. Click, Scarlet is surrounded by amazing guys who touch me deeply. Click, Scarlet is a thief. Click.....<b>Scarlet is truly a <i>badass.</i></b> <br><br><b>My fists were shaking as I ran, sweat pushing out the filth, desperate for the water. I jumped the big rock and dove in, breaking the surface and crashing into fierce cold. <br>I hung there, under the water. My eyes were closed and my skin went fair numb. My lumps and slices went to ice. There were no room for nothing in my mind but cold.<br>When I pulled out of the water, heaving shivery breaths on the shore, I were fearless.</b><br><br>Like....okay....I loved Disney movies. All the fairy tales, all the magic, all the romance (Except for Maleficent from Sleeping Beauty-that creepy bitch was a bit much to take). It was all so intoxicating and alluring-I was spell-bound and attached to the screen whenever one of these amazing movies came on (And <b>Winnie the Pooh-WTP is my home-slice...</b>I'd take him over any fairy tale character any day. I adore Mr. Pooh lol). And, here I am today-a 24 year old girl on the cusp of becoming a wife and hopefully soon starting a family of my own, and I <b>still</b> become a little girl again and again when a Disney movie comes on. I become entranced just as I did when I was a child, the charms of a magical, far-away place still so addicting that I can't help but to play pretend while I dream of Prince Charmings, Prince Erics, and Aladdins in our modern day world. So, I guess it goes without saying that I am a sucker for a well-written (or I guess well advertised, seeing as I haven't read that many fairy tale re-tellings just yet-I'm so picky! Don't ruin my favorites!) re-tellings or renditions or influences of all the childhood classics. <br><br><b>He grabbed my arms, bringing me close to his face, and his eyes looked like the ocean, deep and dark and full of things I knew nothing 'bout. "We don't lie to each other, Scar. Especially not about things that mean I might lose you."<br>My breath froze in my chest. Did he just say that?</b><br><br>But when I think of these movies, for some reason, I don't generally think of Robin Hood. Why is that? I loved it! It was funny, ornery, and just a super-cute movie. But this book?? It brought that memory crashing back to the surface with the force of a hurricane. I felt like a little kid again and, more than that, a really satisfied adult. Seriously. The romance was off the charts, the jealousies were adorable, and the thieving? It was pretty damn cool. And, dare I say, the <b>peril</b> was astounding. Oh yes, this isn't a childhood fantasy anymore. This is the adult version with blood and real thieving and stolen kisses and pain. It isn't like it was gruesome, by any means, but it was just evil enough that I was smiling like the damn Cheshire Cat in the darkness of the bedroom because it was just so damn sinfully delicious! <br><br><b>"Make no mistake," he told me. I looked up. "We do what we do-" He halted, then stepped one foot closer. "I do what I do because I will always believe that no matter how awful life gets for however many of these people, there is something I can do about it. There is something I <i>will</i> do about it."<br>I nodded. "That's why you're the hero, Rob, and I'm a thief."</b><br><br>I still really don't know what to say. How do you convince people to read something that spoke to you in such loud volumes and convey just how good it really is? People, in general, are skeptical of fairy tale re-tellings. I agree-I rarely read them. But, and I say this heavily, this isn't meant to be like the movie from when we were kids. It embodies all the same values-stealing to get taxes gathered up for the poor, getting them food so they can eat, and a few things that I believe to be quite spoilery. My memory is rusty on what the kids' movie was like, but I don't remember a band of merry men. Wasn't it just Robin and John (The fox and the bear)? Anyway, in this book, they have a group! The dynamics of the group were awesome and I loved seeing them support one another, risk their life for one another, poke fun, flirt.....it just <i>worked.</i> And we needed a guy to make Rob jealous, eh?<br><br><b>"Rob, did you hear about Scar's new lover?" John crowed.<br>Rob looked sharp to me. "Was there an old one?"<br>"Jenny Percy!" Much said, pleased with himself.<br>Rob smiled. "Of a band with three actual boys, why is it that all the maids lust after the fake one?"</b><br><br>We have Rob, Scarlet, John, and Much in this rendition. But, in true Chelsea fashion, I shall gush about Rob and Scarlet. Or maybe I'll just break it down for you-Scarlet is a girl (who blushes a lot-but I didn't care-I just. Don't. Flippin'. Care.) who steals for the poor and is the best, most capable thief of the group. She's hard and disguises herself as 'Will Scarlet' so people believe she is merely a boy. She is hiding from someone-someone evil who only wishes to kill her...and anyone who stands in his path. Then there's my darling Robin Hood. He is better known as Rob or 'The Hood' by the townspeople or anyone looking to arrest or track them down. He got this little group together and is the leader because of his kind and giving nature, and his will to atone for his past misgivings. Let's call it what it is: they are in love with one another but are too stubborn to admit it. And pesky John keeps getting in the way-I love you John, but <b>back the fuck off.</b> <br><br><b>I turned out the back way then; there weren't much more to say.<br>He caught my wrist before I were full out the door. "Scar," he said, rough, like rocks were running over his tongue. "I have done so many unforgivable things in my life. Don't let failing to save you be another."</b><br><br>I believe the tension, the angst, the jealous and scorching looks that are spread throughout the novel are what made me the happiest. They broke my heart and sucked me in, making me a prisoner of the story. And the best part, which I haven't told you yet, is that when they were separated or there was no romance, I STILL couldn't put this shit down. I mean, every expedition or haul was just as exciting as the romance. It was exhilarating and fresh and toxic-they were on the run, the guards wanted to catch them, torture them, kill them for their stealing, so each time they left the safety of their hideouts, there was always a chance one could be captured and made to pay. And the other other best part??? <b>No one was immune. No one escaped unscathed in one form or another....and it only got more and more intense.</b><br><br><b>She shook her head. "They would have pinched you too, and then where would Robin be?"<br>"He'd be right as rain, I think."<br>She chuckled. "You don't see how much he cares about you, but he does. Ran into that fire last night like a fair angel, he did."<br>"He'd do the same for one of his men, or any of his people. Don't make me special in his eyes." It were shameful, but there were a fair amount of bitter in my voice.<br>She leaned her head close to mine so the others wouldn't overhear her. "Ah, he has many men, but he only has one woman."</b><br><br>Oh, the writing, real quick. Amazing, quick-witted, error free, and vivid writing. And despite the way Scarlet speaks ('he were' instead of using 'he was' is a prime example), there isn't a mistake to be seen. I had so much fun reading about the different ways they speak and what she is willing to do to survive. You might be shocked, and you might not. But I loved it all, even the way she butchered her speech....and I'm a stickler for, at least, decent grammar.<br><br><b>"You lied to me tonight," John said.<br>I shrugged. "I lie to you a lot. Reckon you might want to be more specific."<br>"You said you'd wait at the top. You said we'd go together."<br>"Well, yes, that was a lie."</b><br><br>So, if someone were to ask me if I would recommend this, I'd give a million enthusiastic thumbs up. It won't work for everyone, the writing ensures that, but some of you will be like me-you'll pick this up, you'll think, 'eh', and then you will fall-<b>hard.</b> You won't realize you're obsessed with it or that you think about it constantly or that you are staying up <b>way too late</b> (Ummm thus the hardcore bags under my eyes) just to get 'one more chapter in'...all because you fell in love with this book. And you won't remember <b>when</b> or <b>how</b> or <b>why</b>....but you'll realize something: Robin Hood stole your heart. Just like he did, mine.<br><br><br>******************************************<br><br><b>Aaaah Okay I never do this but....when I listen to this song it TOTALLY makes me think of this book and I <b>have</b> to share it:<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vdJOlhJH9UE">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vdJOl...</a><br><b>Love Love LOVE IT! ♥</b> (but not as much as this book)</b><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/%20" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="60" width="139" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409285880i/10960212.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129877587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3724105571628096948">I simply adore these books! I've read them twice now, and can;t help but picking them up from time to time to re-read my favourite sections.<br/><br/>Scarlet follows the story of Will Scarlet, one of the heroes of the Robin Hood legend, but who is actually a girl in disguise. She has joined Robin's band of Merry Men, but is keeping her true identity a secret. Once the Sheriff invites the infamous Guy of Gisbourne to Nottingham to rid the county of Robin once and for all, Scarlet finds herself risking her </span>
  <span id="freeText3724105571628096948" style="display:none">I simply adore these books! I've read them twice now, and can;t help but picking them up from time to time to re-read my favourite sections.<br /><br />Scarlet follows the story of Will Scarlet, one of the heroes of the Robin Hood legend, but who is actually a girl in disguise. She has joined Robin's band of Merry Men, but is keeping her true identity a secret. Once the Sheriff invites the infamous Guy of Gisbourne to Nottingham to rid the county of Robin once and for all, Scarlet finds herself risking her life, and her identity, in order to save others, and protect Nottingham.<br /><br />Scarlet is honestly the best heroine I have ever read in historical fiction. Gaughen obviously did her research to make the story appear so realistic, it was as if you were actually with Scarlet and the gang on their adventures. Scarlet embodied everything I know about this period, and though she kept as much of herself a secret as she could, there was a vulnerable side to her, one which came out the most when she was with Rob. No matter what it would do to herself, she would risk her life to save innocents, especially when Guy is turning up the pressure to discover her.<br /><br />Like I said, everything about the world building and writing style just improved the book even more. The description of Nottingham and Sherwood made everything come to life, and I loved how everything just flowed naturally - nothing seemed out of place. Guy was a piece of work, but in a way that showed he might just have some humanity about him, and there was a reason behind his anger.<br /><br />The romance is infinitesimal, but its more a slow burn which make your heart ache, but also means you have the biggest grin on your face. Robin and Scarlet are perfect for each other, but they both have their demons, and their secrets, and don't trust themselves enough to let someone else in. The way Rob knew that Scarlet would reveal more about herself and her past when she was ready, you just knew that they were the best for one another.<br /><br />The ending of this book means you need Lady Thief immediately. I found the revelation of her identity done in the best way, though everyone knows who Scarlet actually is. If you're a fan of Robin Hood in any form, or historical fiction, this is definitely a book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3724105571628096948" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10878513327969328793" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1431607013i/14853139._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▧ Take a <b>badass female lead</b> who knows how to throw a knife and whose snarky inner comments made me laugh - but <b>who blushes way too much</b> for <i>no reasons</i>.<br><br>► <u>Give her a good shake</u> : there's hope for her in the sequel, I hope, I <i>know</i> it. <br><br><i>She only has to let go of her split personality and I'll truly appreciate her. </i><br><br>Just sayin'.<br><br>▧ Take a <b>fantastic past earl who becomes the archetype of the broody but selfless hero</b> - you know, <i>Robin Hood</i>, who made my heart beat like crazy thanks to his full awesomeness <i>annnnd</i> hotness - who I'd follow anywhere as much as I loved him. <i>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284460392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12454008024388963506">I don't usually give star ratings for novels anymore, simply because I know how much soul goes into creating and publishing a book. But with SCARLET, I couldn't NOT give this debut 5 whopping stars. This is the BEST novel I've read in a very very long time. It had me completely sucked in from chapter one, and I didn't want it to end when the last page crept up. <br/>Scarlet is a fabulously complex girl. I loved her so much--strong and independent, with demons in her past and a fearful secret revolvin</span>
  <span id="freeText12454008024388963506" style="display:none">I don't usually give star ratings for novels anymore, simply because I know how much soul goes into creating and publishing a book. But with SCARLET, I couldn't NOT give this debut 5 whopping stars. This is the BEST novel I've read in a very very long time. It had me completely sucked in from chapter one, and I didn't want it to end when the last page crept up. <br />Scarlet is a fabulously complex girl. I loved her so much--strong and independent, with demons in her past and a fearful secret revolving around Guy of Gisbourne (I couldn't help but picture the devilishly handsome Richard Armitage from the BBC show, even though I love Richard and detested Gisbourne).<br />A.C. balanced plot and action, and a rich and mature love triangle so well. Robin and Little John were both characters to root for. I need there to be another Scarlet novel in the works ;-) I will be anxiously awaiting A.C.'s next novel no matter what! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12454008024388963506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_140190061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140190061" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3575414-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507484856p2/3575414.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140190061?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/3575414-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140190061" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3571079261574166509">I opened this book, and after reading the dialect, I thought, "Huh...I'm not sure I'll be able to read this..." Then, three pages later, I was so sucked into the story, I stopped noticing the dialect. All I saw was Scarlet's VOICE--and let me tell you, she <i>has</i> one. A powerful, compelling, stubborn-as-hell voice that fits every impulsive, disgruntled course of action she chooses.<br/><br/>To be honest, impulsive MCs are pretty common (erm...my own...::coughcough::), but Scarlet is easily the most <i>convincin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3571079261574166509" style="display:none">I opened this book, and after reading the dialect, I thought, "Huh...I'm not sure I'll be able to read this..." Then, three pages later, I was so sucked into the story, I stopped noticing the dialect. All I saw was Scarlet's VOICE--and let me tell you, she <i>has</i> one. A powerful, compelling, stubborn-as-hell voice that fits every impulsive, disgruntled course of action she chooses.<br /><br />To be honest, impulsive MCs are pretty common (erm...my own...::coughcough::), but Scarlet is easily the most <i>convincing</i> impulsive MC I've ever seen. She's short-tempered, but only because she's got some pretty big demons haunting her past. She's emotional and deeply moved to help those in need, and best of all, she's 100% kickbutt. SHE THROWS <i>KNIVES!</i> O_O<br /><br />Honestly, though, the highlight of the story for me was the romance. I was just so, so, sooooo torn between John Little and Robin. I won't tell you which boy she chooses, but I will say that I was utterly, <i>utterly</i> satisfied with her choice. And every scene she spends with that boy had my heart pounding and my lips grinning.<br /><br />So, if you're in the mood for Robin-Hood-adventure, swoon-worthy romance, or a tough-as-nails heroine, then be sure to pick up A.C. Gaughen's SCARLET.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3571079261574166509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1543839146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543839146" />
    <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog"><img alt="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576986930p2/28353412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543839146?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=insta-not-used">insta-not-used</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=sigh-bbf">sigh-bbf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=good-boys-i-love">good-boys-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed">romance-forbidden-or-starcrossed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=go-away-sweaty-palms">go-away-sweaty-palms</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543839146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10549925954862094064"><b>Scarlet was an adventurous story that was filled to the brim with excitement and hardships at many turns.</b>  I was a little nervous stepping into a book that contained characters that I hold near and dear to my heart, but <b>I loved how Scarlet felt familiar yet was uniquely different at the same time!  </b>While I did have some issues with a love triangle, I can't wait to see what happens with the rest of this trilogy.  Especially after that fabulous life and death ending!<br/><blockquote>
  <b>I swallowed. “We watch each </b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10549925954862094064" style="display:none"><b>Scarlet was an adventurous story that was filled to the brim with excitement and hardships at many turns.</b>  I was a little nervous stepping into a book that contained characters that I hold near and dear to my heart, but <b>I loved how Scarlet felt familiar yet was uniquely different at the same time!  </b>While I did have some issues with a love triangle, I can't wait to see what happens with the rest of this trilogy.  Especially after that fabulous life and death ending!<br><blockquote>
  <b>I swallowed. “We watch each others’ backs.”<br>He nodded. “Precisely.”</b>
</blockquote><br>One of my favorite changes to this story is the addition of a female in Robin Hood's group.  She goes by Will Scarlet, or Scar as their little band call her.  The majority of the townspeople believe that she is a boy, but a select few know her secret.  And it was so much fun seeing the female being painted as the thief within their group!  As someone who loves females with a backbone and can stand on their own, I was ecstatic with Robin Hood's possible love interest.  In the previous stories, <b>Robin Hood was always paired with a woman who needs to be rescued or taken care of, which always bothered me.  Robin Hood deserves a fighter, a woman who can be his equal and stand by his side!  And while Scarlet is that woman, there's one small problem.  She really isn't his.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>".....if you stay, I’ll keep you safe as best I can.” - Rob to Scar</b>
</blockquote><br>And here lies <b>my struggle with this book and Scarlet.  She tested my patience time and time again by showing interest in both John (aka John Little) and Rob (aka Robin Hood). </b> I felt as though she toyed with them throughout the story.  BUT toy <em>isn't</em> the correct word because she is only 18 and doesn't have any experience with love or relationships.  Yet I was left feeling as though I wanted to shake her while yelling at her to make up her mind.  But <b>I still liked Scarlet because her heart was in the right place so many times.  Not only by protecting the townspeople, but her little group too.  </b>She put her life on the line for so many of them again and again, which made for some amazing perilous situations.<br><blockquote>
  <b>He caught my wrist before I were full out the door. “Scar,” he said, rough, like rocks were running over his tongue. “I have done so many unforgivable things in my life. Don’t let failing to save you be another.”</b>
</blockquote><br>And while I'm talking about struggles, some may have a few issues with the writing.  But please know that <strong>I absolutely adored the way this story was written!</strong> <b> </b>I easily adapted into how the words came across, and<b> it seemed like a unique mix of past, present, and dialect that would easily be found from that time period.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>He pressed my cheek with the cloth again, and then his hand touched my cheek, hot after the cold water. “I hate seeing you hurt.”<br>The air whooshed from my chest but I rolled my eyes ’stead of letting on. “No one gets all bent up over John being bruised.”<br>He stepped back, looking into my eyes. I felt like my eyes were unprotected without my hat.<br>“Scar, you walked in here covered in blood. You don’t see how that would upset us?”<br>“No.”<br>He caught my chin in his fingers. “Like it or not, Scar, we’re your friends. We care about you. I care about you.”</b>
</blockquote><br>You know what else I loved?  <b>Rob!  He was quiet yet powerful, and he had a heart of gold.  He tried so hard to take care of others who weren't able to care for themselves.  And he wore their pain and suffering heavily on his shoulders, while keeping it all to himself.  </b>It even felt as though he purposely contradicted himself so others wouldn't know how he felt.  He did this multiple times with Scarlet, and I was dying to know the truth and his inner thoughts!  I can't wait to learn more about Rob as the trilogy unfolds!<br><blockquote>
  <b>He grabbed my arms, bringing me close to his face, and his eyes looked like the ocean, deep and dark and full of things I knew nothing ’bout. “We don’t lie to each other, Scar. Especially not about things that mean I might lose you.”<br>My breath froze in my chest. Did he just say that?<br>He let me go. “Because losing one member would put the whole band at risk. Do you understand?”</b>
</blockquote><br><b>John and Much rounded out their little group, and the story proceeds with them trying to protect the townspeople from the evil Sheriff of Nottingham.  </b>Their group of four steal and loot all in the name of the greater good, yet twists unfold that take a typical Robin Hood story-line into another area.  Because <b>Scarlet is being hunted by an evil Lord, Gisbourne.  And with him close on their tails, everything is about to spiral out of control.</b>  This is definitely a world you should step into.  And I can't wait to see what is going to happen after that fabulous, perilous ending!!<br><br>P.S. Random fact - I absolutely adore the Disney and Robin Hood:Prince of Thieves movies, so with those story-lines floating around in my head, I dove right into Scarlet.  This story was just as unique as those two movies are from each other.  I'm so very happy about that!<br><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/2016/02/book-review-scarlet-scarlet-1-by-a-c-gaughen-2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">This review was originally posted on Star-Crossed Book Blog</a><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i> <br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287496i/17673736._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>

<div id="review_233286867" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233286867" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233286867?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Angie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1178469-emily-coleman">Emily Coleman</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=girls-who-do-things">girls-who-do-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=something-special">something-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233286867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10216624130990328964">Okay. You are all familiar with my . . . what's the word . . . <i>thing</i> . . . for thieves. And Robin is perhaps the thief I've loved the longest. So it should come as no surprise when I say that I was <i>filled with glee</i> when I first heard about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4573275.A_C__Gaughen' title='A.C. Gaughen' rel='nofollow noopener'>A. C. Gaughen</a>'s upcoming retelling--SCARLET. I liked the cover and, without running down too many spoilery details, I looked forward to the focus on Will Scarlet and the fact that it hailed from a debut author. All of these things add up to that most wonderful</span>
  <span id="freeText10216624130990328964" style="display:none">Okay. You are all familiar with my . . . what's the word . . . <i>thing</i> . . . for thieves. And Robin is perhaps the thief I've loved the longest. So it should come as no surprise when I say that I was <i>filled with glee</i> when I first heard about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4573275.A_C__Gaughen" title="A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">A. C. Gaughen</a>'s upcoming retelling--SCARLET. I liked the cover and, without running down too many spoilery details, I looked forward to the focus on Will Scarlet and the fact that it hailed from a debut author. All of these things add up to that most wonderful of things--possibility. I've reviewed both my favorite Robin Hood retellings here already. And I've read quite a few more. They have all been interesting reads aimed at a variety of types and ages of readers. This particular one is being marketed YA, and I wondered idly, as I anticipated the book, what form my beloved characters would take in this incarnation.<br /><br />Scarlet is a thief. And a liar. She's a thief and a liar and about twenty different kinds of deadly with her knives. And she's loyal to one person on this earth and one person only--Robin Hood. Also known as Robin of Locksley or (less commonly now) the Earl Huntingdon, Robin gave her a place and a hood to hide behind when Scarlet needed it the most, and now she forms an integral member of his band in Sherwood Forest. Standing up to the ruthless Sheriff of Nottingham, Robin, Scarlet, and the lads (Little John and Much) are determined to spare the good folk of Nottinghamshire from the sheriff's wrath for as long as it takes. Outside of her three comrades, few folk have any idea Scarlet is a girl. The boys refer to her as Will, and she has no intention of disobliging anyone of that particular notion. You see, Robin is not the only one with demons in his past. And when the sheriff goes and hires the dreaded Guy of Gisbourne to hunt down the Hood and his band, Scarlet knows her days may at last be numbered. It's only a matter of time before her past catches up with her, and then even Robin's protection may not be enough to keep her from the hangman's noose.<br /><br />SCARLET is massively entertaining. I was caught up in this unusual thief's story from the first page. At the point in which we meet her, Scarlet herself is eighteen years old. The same age as John and just a couple or three years younger than Rob (I love that she calls him Rob). This age spread worked nicely as Robin is home from the crusades--an old man in a young man's body--and Scarlet herself is an old soul, having prowled the streets of London before Rob hauled her off to Sherwood to join his noble cause. These two broken youths find something akin to hope in each other despite the harshness of their previous lives, and I can't tell you how many times my heart contracted with sympathy for them. The characters in SCARLET like to keep their secrets. Every one of them is holding onto something they'd prefer not come out into the light of day. Nobody more than Scarlet herself, of course, but I appreciated the various histories and enjoyed the ways in which <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4573275.A_C__Gaughen" title="A.C. Gaughen" rel="nofollow noopener">A. C. Gaughen</a> incorporated the many traditional threads of the tale. I'm always a fan of girls in disguise, and this one has the bite to match her bark, if you will. She has few soft spots--possibly just the one--and that one is so rife with impossibility and unspoken hope that it hardly warrants the name. But I happily plunged into those impossible hopes with her and adopted them as my own. Which is to say, Scarlet had my affections from the get go. The boys I liked at first and grew to love (and sometimes hate) as the game unfolded. I like that Robin isn't portrayed perfectly. Don't get me wrong. He's a hero through and through. But he has his fair share of shortsightedness. And ghosts. And I wasn't always sure he deserved the ending I wanted for him. I also wished for a bit more complexity on the part of the villain. There was so much potential for Gisbourne in this retelling, and I felt as though he came off a bit, well, ridiculous at times, when he should have been terrifying. But despite these smallish quibbles, I stayed up hours past my bedtime devouring the final chapters in this delightful debut. If you're at all a fan of Robin Hood and women who know their way around a weapon, you won't want to miss it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10216624130990328964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267708813" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267708813" />
    <a title="Diana Stormblessed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6780660-diana-stormblessed"><img alt="Diana Stormblessed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524966495p2/6780660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267708813?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana Stormblessed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana Stormblessed" href="/user/show/6780660-diana-stormblessed">Diana Stormblessed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6780660-diana-stormblessed?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6780660-diana-stormblessed?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267708813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3095482331903853617">I am a sucker for a good historical retelling, and a strong heroine to be honest, and this book had everything I was looking for.<br/><br/>Scarlet is a member of Robin Hood's band of thieves. Few outside the group know that she's a girl, as she disguises herself as Will Scarlet. In the legends and movies of past Robin Hoods, Will was often considered Robin's best friend, and was always played by the cutest, dorkiest boys. In case you need a reminder:<br/><br/>Robin Hood: Prince of Thieves (1991)<br/><a href='http://s1082.photobucket.com/albums/j361/dashichka1/?action=view&current=WillScarletSlater.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368279i/720832.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Robin Hood: Men </span>
  <span id="freeText3095482331903853617" style="display:none">I am a sucker for a good historical retelling, and a strong heroine to be honest, and this book had everything I was looking for.<br><br>Scarlet is a member of Robin Hood's band of thieves. Few outside the group know that she's a girl, as she disguises herself as Will Scarlet. In the legends and movies of past Robin Hoods, Will was often considered Robin's best friend, and was always played by the cutest, dorkiest boys. In case you need a reminder:<br><br>Robin Hood: Prince of Thieves (1991)<br><a href="http://s1082.photobucket.com/albums/j361/dashichka1/?action=view&amp;current=WillScarletSlater.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368279i/720832.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Robin Hood: Men in Tights (1993)<br><a href="http://s1082.photobucket.com/albums/j361/dashichka1/?action=view&amp;current=WillScarletMeninTights.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368279i/720833.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Oh, and while there was no Will character in the Disney version of Robin Hood, I think it was by far my favorite, and I still encourage you to go see it.<br><br><a href="http://s1082.photobucket.com/albums/j361/dashichka1/?action=view&amp;current=WillScarletDisney.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368279i/720834.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Anyway, in this version Scarlet is a girl with a past. She's been hiding out with Robin's men for the past two years, but now the Sheriff has hired the thief-taker Gisbourne to bring Robin in once and for all. With Gisbourne's arrival, the past that Scarlet has fought to keep hidden for all these years is threatening to reveal itself.<br><br>This story is written beautifully. Its written in Scarlet's words, with her commoner accent, the way she would have talked back in those days. The plot stars off action filled and never gets dull. The character development was wonderful, as well as the richness in the way the different character relationships were laid out.<br><br>Speaking of the characters, they by far they were what made this such a wonderful story. Each had their flaws. <br><br>Scarlet is running from her past. She's crude, secretive, and generally keeps to herself. <br><br>Robin has a bit of a temper. Instead of the perfect hero, he's a little rough around the edges. He has the weight of the world on his shoulders, and sometimes that much pressure gets to be a bit much. He might be the most realistic Robin Hood I've read/seen. <br><br>Little John is a big, charismatic brute. He was definitely more attractive here than in other stories. <br><br>Much is the youngest and sweetest member of the group. Scarlet cares for him like a brother.<br><br>Even the secondary characters, the townspeople, where wonderful. They had weak moments, but they were just human. All coping with the crummy situations they were in.<br><br>And yes, there was even a little romance. But it was the kind I really like. The romance was secondary in the story. It was something in the background, just teasing you without ever overriding the main plot. I don't want to say too much, but I love a good romance tease.<br><br>The only problem I had with the book was that its a stand alone book. The ending, while wrapping up the plot, still leaves loose ends with so much room for a sequel. Its a great place to stop to make you want more. And I do. I'm hoping for a sequel, because without one, that ending is just going to kill me.<br><br>For more reviews check out <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://nightlyreading.wordpress.com/">http://nightlyreading.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3095482331903853617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/996786617" />
    <a title="Teryna90" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7040410-teryna90"><img alt="Teryna90" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455020920p2/7040410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/996786617?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2014</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15311396482952209682"> The first thing that came to mind as soon as I figured out this was about Robin Hood's band was the <i>Robin Hood</i> song that the italian cartoon singer Cristina D'avena sang, here's the link if you'd like to listen to it, it's really adorable: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MVdXxxXMcxY'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MVdXx...</a>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424254937ra/13734176.gif' width='500' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>. <br/>I grew up with Robin Hood's cartoons and soon fell in love with all the movies and the stories... and when I found out that one of my fav author had actually wrotten Robin Hood, not only did I feel stupid but also e</span>
  <span id="freeText15311396482952209682" style="display:none"> The first thing that came to mind as soon as I figured out this was about Robin Hood's band was the <i>Robin Hood</i> song that the italian cartoon singer Cristina D'avena sang, here's the link if you'd like to listen to it, it's really adorable: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MVdXxxXMcxY">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MVdXx...</a>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424254937ra/13734176.gif" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>. <br>I grew up with Robin Hood's cartoons and soon fell in love with all the movies and the stories... and when I found out that one of my fav author had actually wrotten Robin Hood, not only did I feel stupid but also enthusiastic. I went out and bought Dumas' Robin Hood and after reading it I just couldn't stop holding it and smiling! Even though Lady Marion dies, I was prepared for her death but it still hurt. And right now I'm hoping that the author that did not like the weak figure of Marion will actually change the ending ^^, well <i>Scarlet is no weak Marion. </i><br><br>A hero who steals from rich to give to poor, to help them pay taxes ^^ we can't help falling in love with someone like that! Even if its just a tale, a myth, a book character! Just can't help it, and Gaughen's Robin seems even more handsome!<br><br>I really really loved this book, and I'm happy because it's not easy to pick up a tale like Robin Hood and internalize it like A.C. Gaughen has done. She on my advice has done a marvellous job. At first I must admit I had a hard time getting used to Scarlet's language, it sounded forced and annoying and so no natural, and I think that was the author's purpose. Let's not forget who Scarlet is. A Lady.<br><br>We have a story set in our favorite forest, Sherwood and we find most of the characters loyal to Robin like little John, here John little, Much; Friar Tuck and Lady Marion, that takes the name of one of the characters, Will Scarlet. We don't find a lady like Marion but a thief, forced to steal to live at first and then forced to live to steal goods that could help others survive. It's clear like the rain that she is totally head over feat for our hero, Robin Hood, even though she has a hard time figuring it out. Stupid Scarlet! There is also another one falling slowly in love with Marion, cus we already know that "our" Robin is totally lost over her, and that is John little. His parts weren't annoying at all, I actually liked him a lot and fell pretty sorry for him... Well we will see what will happen in book two between them and how things are going to get tensed in the band. And I also hope that the author gives us a good love or happy story for John, he really deserves it.<br><br>I liked the adventures, the fighting, it wasn't much but it was good. I liked the descriptions and the feeling that the dialogues made me feel. I lost a couple of heart beat along the reading and just couldn't help it. Robin melts our hearts with his words and then shatters Scarlet's hope, but we know why he does and says what he does. &lt;3 Our hero &lt;3 *.*<br><br>I love it when books make my heart melt. <br><br><i>"We don't lie to each other, Scar. Especially not about things that mean I might lose you."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424255998ra/13734333.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Some spoilers - - After finishing this book I just wanted to start the second as soon as possible. Lady Marion wed to that little mean rat, the sheriff dead, Robin and Scarlet hugging, I wanted to know more and read more but I decided to wait for book three, I don't feel like not only suffering after book two but also being forced to wait months before book three comes out, no way! Pure torture!<br></span>

<div id="review_614471508" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/614471508" />
    <a title="Lauren (Sugar &amp; Snark)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2129552-lauren-sugar-snark"><img alt="Lauren (Sugar &amp; Snark)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354536337p2/2129552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/614471508?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren (Sugar &amp; Snark)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren (Sugar &amp; Snark)" href="/user/show/2129552-lauren-sugar-snark">Lauren (Sugar &amp; Snark)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2129552-lauren-sugar-snark?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2129552-lauren-sugar-snark?shelf=mishmash">mishmash</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer614471508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17067595992244314203"><a href='http://www.freesmileys.org/smileys.php' title='Smiley' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391129i/753236.gif' alt='Smiley' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a>	<br/>First let me just say that I am a huge fan of the Robin Hood Legend. As a kid I watched the Kevin Costner, Morgan Freeman movie about 15 times more then most people would call healthy. So when I saw there was a book out that had a twist on the same old story –<b> Will Scarlet is a girl in disguise!!!</b> I was beyond excited.<br/> <br/><b>But then it turned out to be just so BAD!! </b><br/><br/><b>Here’s why-</b><br/>Let me paint a picture of Scarlet for you - Imagine that chick from Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon who can fly through t</span>
  <span id="freeText17067595992244314203" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.freesmileys.org/smileys.php" title="Smiley" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391129i/753236.gif" alt="Smiley" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>	<br>First let me just say that I am a huge fan of the Robin Hood Legend. As a kid I watched the Kevin Costner, Morgan Freeman movie about 15 times more then most people would call healthy. So when I saw there was a book out that had a twist on the same old story –<b> Will Scarlet is a girl in disguise!!!</b> I was beyond excited.<br> <br><b>But then it turned out to be just so BAD!! </b><br><br><b>Here’s why-</b><br>Let me paint a picture of Scarlet for you - Imagine that chick from Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon who can fly through trees and has other seemingly super human powers but with knives instead of swords. (Scarlet thinks swords suck!) Now make her a martyr (not in a good way) and give her a persecution complex topped off with an eating disorder. Oh and just to round it all off she is also a compulsive spitter with a tendency to brag. What a winner right?? (go girl power)<br><br><b>I personally found very little to like about this girl.</b> When she wasn’t doing acrobatics through the forest?? Or utilising her kick ass thieving skills (not as kick ass as the author/Scarlet would have us believe)<b> she is either sulking or leading Robin and his merry men around by the cocks. </b> In fact the story may as well have been changed to Scarlet and her merry men. Because the way this story portrayed it Scarlet was the one with<i> all </i>the plans, <i> all </i>the skills and the one that <i> always</i>saves the day. In fact Robin was basically only there as eye candy and to be a pawn in Scarlet’s love triangle. Yes CRINGE there is a love triangle!!<br><br>This book was written in the first person and I have to say that <b>I have never read a more bizarre attempt at a British/colloquial/I just don’t know what accent. It was actually painful to read.</b> And more importantly why was Scarlet the only person in the whole book with an accent?? From the lowliest peasant to the highest Lord everyone spoke perfect English. So what the hell??!! I think it took me twice as long to read this book then it should have, just because I was constantly trying to figure out what tense it was in! And I won’t even go into the author’s terrible habit of constantly stating the obvious! <br><br>As for the plot, predictable is too mild a word. And on top of this the book is littered with historical inaccuracies. But perhaps worst of all, as I mentioned briefly before <b>Robin Hood has been relegated to a bit part in his own story! I realise the book is called Scarlet but COME ON a line has to be drawn somewhere.</b> The guy at least deserved a little dimension! But now that I think about it none of the other “supporting“ cast member had any dimension either....<br><br>So in summation, there are lots of great Robin Hood stories out there but IMHO this is not one of them. <b>This book doesn’t add anything new or interesting to the legend and I honestly wish I had just skipped it.</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17067595992244314203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Trisha Wolfe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4378990-trisha-wolfe"><img alt="Trisha Wolfe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502379332p2/4378990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267020490?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trisha Wolfe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trisha Wolfe" href="/user/show/4378990-trisha-wolfe">Trisha Wolfe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267020490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5187503862913280834">Oh, this so my kind of story. A stubborn, brash, get-out-of-my-way-and-let-me-do-my-thing lead character, who is flawed realistically, yet fierce, brave and determined—Scarlet is a strong lead who had me rooting for her the whole time. The only girl among Robin Hood’s band of thieves, she hides away, playing the role of a young boy, while her past is steadily sneaking up on her in the form of a Thief Taker named Lord Gisbourne.Though she doesn't let that hold her back from trying to help the cit</span>
  <span id="freeText5187503862913280834" style="display:none">Oh, this so my kind of story. A stubborn, brash, get-out-of-my-way-and-let-me-do-my-thing lead character, who is flawed realistically, yet fierce, brave and determined—Scarlet is a strong lead who had me rooting for her the whole time. The only girl among Robin Hood’s band of thieves, she hides away, playing the role of a young boy, while her past is steadily sneaking up on her in the form of a Thief Taker named Lord Gisbourne.Though she doesn't let that hold her back from trying to help the citizens of Nottinghamshire. And I loved how she fumbled along her way, but learned, growing in the process.<br /><br />What I also loved about this story was the voice. Gaughen did an amazing job making me feel as if I were back in the time of the Crusades, and Scarlet’s dialect was authentic. I wasn’t expecting much romance, so I was pleasantly surprised when both Robin and Little John seemed to be developing affections for Scarlet. This added more tension to the plot, and I loved every minute of their banter. Scarlet is addicting, and with its twists, secrets, and reveals, it’s a must read for anyone looking to be swept away into an original tale.</span>

Gaugher is writing it so good, I love Robin, John and Much and Scarlet is an amazing badass girl ;) I know I have given many books lately 5 starts but I guess I have had an good book year ^^<br /><br />Re-read before Lady Thief, I just love this book and Robin Hood &lt;3 Just aww, I love Robin, John, Much and Scarlet!! I can't wait to start Lady Thief and I hope it is as good ;)&lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="2835432458926095976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_456446466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/456446466" />
    <a title="Joy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3213955-joy"><img alt="Joy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1354897507p2/3213955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/456446466?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy" href="/user/show/3213955-joy">Joy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer456446466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17924699986515729685">Recently a friend introduced me to the term "Mary Sue" or "Gary Stu" <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue'>http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue</a><br/>I wasn't sure what that meant until I read Scarlet. A female character a "Mary Sue" or male "Gary Stu" is an impossible character. They can do no wrong, everyone loves them, everyone needs them, they know everything and can do it all better than anyone.<br/>I'm a Robin Hood fan. I thought the idea behind Scarlet was promising. A different take on the legend. Will Scarlet actually being a female, </span>
  <span id="freeText17924699986515729685" style="display:none">Recently a friend introduced me to the term "Mary Sue" or "Gary Stu" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue</a><br />I wasn't sure what that meant until I read Scarlet. A female character a "Mary Sue" or male "Gary Stu" is an impossible character. They can do no wrong, everyone loves them, everyone needs them, they know everything and can do it all better than anyone.<br />I'm a Robin Hood fan. I thought the idea behind Scarlet was promising. A different take on the legend. Will Scarlet actually being a female, on the run from a secret, troubling past sounds intriguing, right? Apparently not. Not in the hands of A.C Gaughen anyway. I have no problem with strong female characters. That's actually something I look for in a book, movie, tv show wherever I can find them. But in every character male or female there should be balance. <br />Scarlet was beautiful, smart, talented, desired, self-sacrificing to the max. Robin Hood and the others couldn't rob from the rich and give to the poor properly without her. She knew who to trust and who not to trust. She could hunt, fight, run through the trees and climb like no other. She was the best with a knife and could sneak in and out of the prison, she came up with all the plans to free the people before they were executed, including Robin Hood himself. So I have a question: Why is Robin Hood and his Band of Men in this story at all?! All Nottingham really needs is Scarlet! Not to mention the self-recriminations were rife in this book!<br />I will say that I did like the supporting characters even the Sheriff and Guy of Gisbourne. Liked not loved. They were more like extras than supporting characters at times but I enjoyed them for the most part.<br />Also I was throughly annoyed with Scarlet's grammar in this book. It made no sense to me. I assume it was supposed to be the form of English spoken at the time. However I'm pretty sure it was closer to "redneck" than "medieval". It does take more than replacing 'was' with 'were' and cutting off the bits of a word or two, doesn't it? Here's a bit from the very first chapter: "So I'm a girl. Most people miss that 'bout me. the boys'll call me Will Scarlet if other people are 'bout; a few people know it's just Scarlet. But most think I'm a Will." and "I flicked my eyes over to him, and he were staring at me in that way that I hate, like if he looked long enough he'd see everything I were. "I'm going to throw some knives around."" I read the whole book and that was sticking into my gut the whole time! That is NOT English in any form! I kept trying to give this book a chance but by the end I was sorry I wasted my time. Oh excuse me, I WERE sorry! UGH!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17924699986515729685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16595157621525925358" style="display:none">OMG FLAWLESS BOOK. I LOVE LOVE LOVE IT!!! ♥ Since childhood i always had an attachment with the story of Robin Hood. and it always felt close to home. And then i read this. and WOW. BRILLIANT TWIST. <br /><br />Scarlet is such an amazing character. so strong and badass. reading her thoughts made me feel badass. Rob..OH MY GOD. GIVE ME MY ROB!!! We should all get a Rob!!! JUST UGHHH I LOVE HIMMMM!!! :P *crazy eyes* . Much,he's an adorable little puppy and smart. John..well when he's not trying to ruin my ship,he's a decent fellow :) <br /><br />A.C.Gaughen rights so beautifully. When i first started reading it,i got confused with the 'were' but then as i got used to Scarlet's language, well after that the book just BOOM sucked me in. The angst between Rob and Scarlet killed me!! Even if i was reading Scarlet's thoughts,and even though she wasn't admitting to anything. I KNEWWWWW!!!! And i also knew about her identity. DUH!!! She HAD to be her :D ♥<br />The scenery,the woods,the constant action..MAGIC. This book was MAGIC. I can't wait to read 'Lady Thief'!!!! I'm in love with these books ♥ </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('POeAM+hSFFa/HX7mYkpoCjiAIFKPMdMQR7QEP1p3wcSM0y9me7x/Aq4/rrNalV6D9oBahvIzGOOX4iUMW/yhog==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DGttzEe4NOuWbiMReN5pD4x+einyCDz+SJ5xOq+9Ppm8X8KZ1FZfv4dM80RAAV+GQn4A/Y8K9w2YyFAJrjZe/w==')})
  }
//]]>
